The answer to this riddle is that <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mstyle mathcolor="green"><mi>C</mi><mi>l</mi><mi>a</mi><mi>i</mi><mi>m</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mn>1.2</mn></mstyle></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\textcolor{green}{Claim \ 1.2}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.69444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.01968em; color: green;">Cl</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="color: green;">aim</span><span class="mspace" style="color: green;"><span style="color: green;">&nbsp;</span></span><span class="mord" style="color: green;">1.2</span></span></span></span></span> talks about what can be done with knowledge of the key <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>k</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">k</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.69444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.03148em;">k</span></span></span></span></span> (Alice &amp; Bob’s perspective). <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mstyle mathcolor="green"><mi>C</mi><mi>l</mi><mi>a</mi><mi>i</mi><mi>m</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mn>1.3</mn></mstyle></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\textcolor{green}{Claim \ 1.3}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.69444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.01968em; color: green;">Cl</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="color: green;">aim</span><span class="mspace" style="color: green;"><span style="color: green;">&nbsp;</span></span><span class="mord" style="color: green;">1.3</span></span></span></span></span> talks about the output distribution of the eavesdrop algorithm, which doesn’t include k (Eve’s perspective). In short, if you know <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>k</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">k</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.69444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.03148em;">k</span></span></span></span></span>, then you can decrypt <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>c</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">c</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.43056em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">c</span></span></span></span></span> to obtain <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>m</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">m</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.43056em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">m</span></span></span></span></span>, if you don’t know <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>k</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">k</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.69444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.03148em;">k</span></span></span></span></span>, then <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>c</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">c</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.43056em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">c</span></span></span></span></span> carries no information about <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>m</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">m</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.43056em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">m</span></span></span></span></span> (in fact, it looks uniformly distributed). This is because <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>m</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">m</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.43056em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">m</span></span></span></span></span>, <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>c</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">c</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.43056em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">c</span></span></span></span></span>, <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>k</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">k</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.69444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.03148em;">k</span></span></span></span></span> are all <em>correlated</em> in a delicate way.<sup class="footnote-ref"><a href="#fn3" id="fnref3">3</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><strong>Isn’t there another paradox?</strong> <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mstyle mathcolor="green"><mi>C</mi><mi>l</mi><mi>a</mi><mi>i</mi><mi>m</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mn>1.3</mn></mstyle></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\textcolor{green}{Claim \ 1.3}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.69444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.01968em; color: green;">Cl</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="color: green;">aim</span><span class="mspace" style="color: green;"><span style="color: green;">&nbsp;</span></span><span class="mord" style="color: green;">1.3</span></span></span></span></span> says that the output of EAVESDROP(<span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>m</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">m</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.43056em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">m</span></span></span></span></span>) doesn’t depend on <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>m</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">m</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.43056em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">m</span></span></span></span></span>, but we can see the eavesdrop algorithm literally using its argument <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>m</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">m</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.43056em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">m</span></span></span></span></span> right there in the last line! The answer to this riddle is perhaps best illustrated by the previous illustrations of the EAVESDROP(<span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mn>010</mn></mstyle></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\textcolor{brown}{010}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.64444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord" style="color: brown;">010</span></span></span></span></span>) and EAVESDROP(<span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mn>111</mn></mstyle></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\textcolor{brown}{111}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.64444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord" style="color: brown;">111</span></span></span></span></span>) distributions. The two tables of values are indeed different (so the choice of <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>m</mi><mo>∈</mo><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mn>010</mn></mstyle><mo separator="true">,</mo><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mn>111</mn></mstyle><mo stretchy="false">}</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">m \in \{\textcolor{brown}{010}, \textcolor{brown}{111}\}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">m</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.277778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∈</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.277778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mopen">{</span><span class="mord" style="color: brown;">010</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.166667em;"></span><span class="mord" style="color: brown;">111</span><span class="mclose">}</span></span></span></span></span> clearly has some effect), but they represent the <em>same probability distribution</em> (since order doesn’t matter). <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mstyle mathcolor="green"><mi>C</mi><mi>l</mi><mi>a</mi><mi>i</mi><mi>m</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mn>1.3</mn></mstyle></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\textcolor{green}{Claim \ 1.3}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.69444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.01968em; color: green;">Cl</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="color: green;">aim</span><span class="mspace" style="color: green;"><span style="color: green;">&nbsp;</span></span><span class="mord" style="color: green;">1.3</span></span></span></span></span> considers only the resulting probability distribution.</li>
<li>You probably think about security in terms of a concrete “goal” for the attacker: recover the key, recover the plaintext, etc. <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mstyle mathcolor="green"><mi>C</mi><mi>l</mi><mi>a</mi><mi>i</mi><mi>m</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mn>1.3</mn></mstyle></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\textcolor{green}{Claim \ 1.3}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.69444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.01968em; color: green;">Cl</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="color: green;">aim</span><span class="mspace" style="color: green;"><span style="color: green;">&nbsp;</span></span><span class="mord" style="color: green;">1.3</span></span></span></span></span> doesn’t really refer to attackers in that way, and it certainly doesn’t specify a goal. Rather, we are thinking about security by comparing to some hypothetical “ideal” world. I would be satisfied if the attacker sees only a source of uniform bits, because in this hypothetical world there are no keys and no plaintexts to recover! <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mstyle mathcolor="green"><mi>C</mi><mi>l</mi><mi>a</mi><mi>i</mi><mi>m</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mn>1.3</mn></mstyle></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\textcolor{green}{Claim \ 1.3}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.69444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.01968em; color: green;">Cl</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="color: green;">aim</span><span class="mspace" style="color: green;"><span style="color: green;">&nbsp;</span></span><span class="mord" style="color: green;">1.3</span></span></span></span></span> says that when we actually use OTP, it looks just like this hypothetical world, from the attacker’s point of view. If we imagine any “goal” at all for the attacker in this kind of reasoning, it’s to detect that ciphertexts don’t follow a uniform distribution. By showing that the attacker can’t even achieve this modest goal, it shows that the attacker couldn’t possibly achieve other, more natural, goals like key recovery and plaintext recovery.</li>
</ul>
<h3 id="limitations">Limitations</h3>
<p>One-time pad is incredibly limited in practice. Most notably:</p>
<ul>
<li>Its keys are as long as the plaintexts they encrypt. This is basically unavoidable (see <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mstyle mathcolor="green"><mi>E</mi><mi>x</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>r</mi><mi>c</mi><mi>i</mi><mi>s</mi><mi>e</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mn>2.11</mn></mstyle></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\textcolor{green}{Exercise \ 2.11}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.68333em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.05764em; color: green;">E</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="color: green;">x</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="color: green;">erc</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="color: green;">i</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="color: green;">se</span><span class="mspace" style="color: green;"><span style="color: green;">&nbsp;</span></span><span class="mord" style="color: green;">2.11</span></span></span></span></span>) and leads to a kind of chicken-and-egg dilemma in practice: If two users want to privately convey a <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>λ</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\lambda</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.69444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">λ</span></span></span></span></span>-bit message, they first need to privately agree on a <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>λ</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\lambda</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.69444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">λ</span></span></span></span></span>-bit string.</li>
<li>A key can be used to encrypt only one plaintext (hence, “one-time” pad); see <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mstyle mathcolor="green"><mi>E</mi><mi>x</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>r</mi><mi>c</mi><mi>i</mi><mi>s</mi><mi>e</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mn>1.6</mn></mstyle></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\textcolor{green}{Exercise \ 1.6}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.68333em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.05764em; color: green;">E</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="color: green;">x</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="color: green;">erc</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="color: green;">i</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="color: green;">se</span><span class="mspace" style="color: green;"><span style="color: green;">&nbsp;</span></span><span class="mord" style="color: green;">1.6</span></span></span></span></span>. Indeed, we can see that the eavesdrop subroutine in <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mstyle mathcolor="green"><mi>C</mi><mi>l</mi><mi>a</mi><mi>i</mi><mi>m</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mn>1.3</mn></mstyle></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\textcolor{green}{Claim \ 1.3}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.69444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.01968em; color: green;">Cl</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="color: green;">aim</span><span class="mspace" style="color: green;"><span style="color: green;">&nbsp;</span></span><span class="mord" style="color: green;">1.3</span></span></span></span></span> provides no way for a caller to guarantee that two plaintexts are encrypted with the same key, so it is not clear how to use <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mstyle mathcolor="green"><mi>C</mi><mi>l</mi><mi>a</mi><mi>i</mi><mi>m</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mn>1.3</mn></mstyle></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\textcolor{green}{Claim \ 1.3}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.69444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.01968em; color: green;">Cl</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="color: green;">aim</span><span class="mspace" style="color: green;"><span style="color: green;">&nbsp;</span></span><span class="mord" style="color: green;">1.3</span></span></span></span></span> to argue about what happens in one-time pad when keys are intentionally reused in this way.</li>
</ul>
<p>Despite these limitations, one-time pad illustrates fundamental ideas that appear in most forms of encryption in this course.</p>
<h3 id="exercises">Exercises</h3>
<p>1.1. The one-time pad encryption of plaintext <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mtext mathvariant="monospace">mario</mtext></mstyle></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\textcolor{brown}{\texttt{mario}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.61111em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord text" style="color: brown;"><span class="mord texttt" style="color: brown;">mario</span></span></span></span></span></span> (when converted from ASCII to binary in the standard way) under key <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>k</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">k</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.69444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.03148em;">k</span></span></span></span></span> is:</p>
<p><span class="katex--display"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mn>1000010000000111010101000001110000011101</mn></mstyle><mi mathvariant="normal">.</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
\textcolor{brown}{1000010000000111010101000001110000011101}.
</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.64444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord" style="color: brown;">1000010000000111010101000001110000011101</span><span class="mord">.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p>
<p>What is the one-time pad encryption of <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mtext mathvariant="monospace">luigi</mtext></mstyle></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\textcolor{brown}{\texttt{luigi}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.83333em; vertical-align: -0.22222em;"></span><span class="mord text" style="color: brown;"><span class="mord texttt" style="color: brown;">luigi</span></span></span></span></span></span> under the same key?</p>
<p>1.2. Alice is using one-time pad and notices that when her key is the all-zeroes string <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>k</mi><mo>=</mo><msup><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mn>0</mn></mstyle><mi>λ</mi></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">k = \textcolor{brown}{0}^{\lambda}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.69444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.03148em;">k</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.277778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.277778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.849108em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord" style="color: brown;">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.849108em;"><span class="" style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">λ</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>, then Enc<span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>k</mi><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi>m</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mo>=</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">(k,m) = m</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.03148em;">k</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.166667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">m</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.277778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.277778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.43056em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">m</span></span></span></span></span> and her message is sent in the clear! To avoid this problem, she decides to modify KeyGen to exclude the all-zeroes key. She modifies KeyGen to choose a key uniformly from <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mn>0</mn></mstyle><mo separator="true">,</mo><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mn>1</mn></mstyle><msup><mo stretchy="false">}</mo><mi>λ</mi></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\{\textcolor{brown}{0}, \textcolor{brown}{1}\}^{\lambda}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.09911em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mopen">{</span><span class="mord" style="color: brown;">0</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.166667em;"></span><span class="mord" style="color: brown;">1</span><span class="mclose"><span class="mclose">}</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.849108em;"><span class="" style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">λ</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> \ <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mn>0</mn></mstyle><msup><mo stretchy="false">}</mo><mi>λ</mi></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\{\textcolor{brown}{0}\}^{\lambda}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.09911em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mopen">{</span><span class="mord" style="color: brown;">0</span><span class="mclose"><span class="mclose">}</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.849108em;"><span class="" style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">λ</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>, the set of all <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>λ</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\lambda</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.69444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">λ</span></span></span></span></span>-bit strings except <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mn>0</mn></mstyle><mi>λ</mi></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\textcolor{brown}{0}^{\lambda}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.849108em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord" style="color: brown;">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.849108em;"><span class="" style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">λ</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>. In this way, she guarantees that her plaintext is never sent in the clear.</p>
<p>Is it still true that the eavesdropper’s ciphertext distribution is uniformly distributed on <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mn>0</mn></mstyle><mo separator="true">,</mo><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mn>1</mn></mstyle><msup><mo stretchy="false">}</mo><mi>λ</mi></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\{\textcolor{brown}{0}, \textcolor{brown}{1}\}^{\lambda}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.09911em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mopen">{</span><span class="mord" style="color: brown;">0</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.166667em;"></span><span class="mord" style="color: brown;">1</span><span class="mclose"><span class="mclose">}</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.849108em;"><span class="" style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">λ</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>? Justify your answer.</p>
<p>1.3. When Alice encrypts the key k itself using one-time pad, the ciphertext will always be the all-zeroes string! So if an eavesdropper sees the all-zeroes ciphertext, she learns that Alice encrypted the key itself. Does this contradict <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mstyle mathcolor="green"><mi>C</mi><mi>l</mi><mi>a</mi><mi>i</mi><mi>m</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mn>1.3</mn></mstyle></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\textcolor{green}{Claim \ 1.3}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.69444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.01968em; color: green;">Cl</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="color: green;">aim</span><span class="mspace" style="color: green;"><span style="color: green;">&nbsp;</span></span><span class="mord" style="color: green;">1.3</span></span></span></span></span>? Why or why not?</p>
<p>1.4. What is so special about defining OTP using the XOR operation? Suppose we use the bitwise-AND operation (which we will write as ‘&amp;’) and define a variant of OTP as follows:</p>
<p><span class="katex--display"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><menclose notation="top bottom left right"><mtable rowspacing="0.6600em" columnalign="left left" columnspacing="1em"><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><munder accentunder="true"><mtext>KeyGen:</mtext><mo stretchy="true">‾</mo></munder></mstyle></mtd><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><munder accentunder="true"><mrow><mtext>Enc&nbsp;(</mtext><mi>k</mi><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi>m</mi><mo>∈</mo><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mn>0</mn></mstyle><mo separator="true">,</mo><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mn>1</mn></mstyle><msup><mo stretchy="false">}</mo><mi>λ</mi></msup><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mo>:</mo></mrow><mo stretchy="true">‾</mo></munder></mstyle></mtd></mtr><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mrow><mspace width="1em"></mspace><mi>k</mi><mo>←</mo><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mn>0</mn></mstyle><mo separator="true">,</mo><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mn>1</mn></mstyle><msup><mo stretchy="false">}</mo><mi>λ</mi></msup></mrow></mstyle></mtd><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mrow><mspace width="1em"></mspace><mrow><mtext>return&nbsp;</mtext><mpadded width="+6pt" height="+6pt" lspace="3pt" voffset="3pt" mathbackground="yellow"><mtext>k&nbsp;&amp;&nbsp;m</mtext></mpadded></mrow></mrow></mstyle></mtd></mtr><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mrow><mspace width="1em"></mspace><mtext>return&nbsp;</mtext><mi>k</mi></mrow></mstyle></mtd></mtr></mtable></menclose></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
\def\arraystretch{1.5} 
\begin{array}{|ll|} \hline 
\underline{\text{KeyGen:}} &amp; \underline{\text{Enc (}k,m \in \{\textcolor{brown}{0},\textcolor{brown}{1}\}^{\lambda}):}\\
\quad k \leftarrow\{\textcolor{brown}{0},\textcolor{brown}{1}\}^{\lambda} &amp; \quad {\text{return } \colorbox{yellow}{k \&amp; m}} \\
\quad \text{return } k \\ \hline
\end{array}
</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 5.44em; vertical-align: -2.45em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 2.99em;"><span class="" style="top: -4.95em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 4.95em;"></span><span class="mtable"><span class="vertical-separator" style="height: 5.4em; border-right-width: 0.04em; border-right-style: solid; margin: 0px -0.02em; vertical-align: -2.45em;"></span><span class="arraycolsep" style="width: 0.5em;"></span><span class="col-align-l"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 2.95em;"><span <p>Is this still a good choice for encryption? Why / why not?</p>
<p>1.5. Describe the aw in this argument:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>Consider the following attack against one-time pad: upon seeing a ciphertext <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>c</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">c</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.43056em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">c</span></span></span></span></span>, the eavesdropper tries every candidate key <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>k</mi><mo>∈</mo><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mn>0</mn></mstyle><mo separator="true">,</mo><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mn>1</mn></mstyle><msup><mo stretchy="false">}</mo><mi>λ</mi></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">k \in \{\textcolor{brown}{0}, \textcolor{brown}{1}\}^{\lambda}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.73354em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.03148em;">k</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.277778em;"></span><span class="mrel">∈</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.277778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.09911em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mopen">{</span><span class="mord" style="color: brown;">0</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.166667em;"></span><span class="mord" style="color: brown;">1</span><span class="mclose"><span class="mclose">}</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.849108em;"><span class="" style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">λ</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> until she has found the one that was used, at which point she outputs the plaintext <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>m</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">m</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.43056em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">m</span></span></span></span></span>. This contradicts the argument in <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mstyle mathcolor="green"><mi>S</mi><mi>e</mi><mi>c</mi><mi>t</mi><mi>i</mi><mi>o</mi><mi>n</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mn>1.2</mn></mstyle></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\textcolor{green}{Section \ 1.2}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.68333em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.05764em; color: green;">S</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="color: green;">ec</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="color: green;">t</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="color: green;">i</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="color: green;">o</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="color: green;">n</span><span class="mspace" style="color: green;"><span style="color: green;">&nbsp;</span></span><span class="mord" style="color: green;">1.2</span></span></span></span></span> that the eavesdropper can obtain no information about <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>m</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">m</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.43056em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">m</span></span></span></span></span> by seeing the ciphertext.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>1.6. Suppose Alice encrypts two plaintexts <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>m</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">m</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.43056em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">m</span></span></span></span></span> and <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mi>m</mi><mo mathvariant="normal" lspace="0em" rspace="0em">′</mo></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">m'</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.751892em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">m</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.751892em;"><span class="" style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">′</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> using one-time pad with the same key <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>k</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">k</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.69444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.03148em;">k</span></span></span></span></span>. What information about <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>m</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">m</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.43056em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">m</span></span></span></span></span> and <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mi>m</mi><mo mathvariant="normal" lspace="0em" rspace="0em">′</mo></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">m'</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.751892em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">m</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.751892em;"><span class="" style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">′</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> is leaked to an eavesdropper by doing this (assume the eavesdropper knows that Alice has reused <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>k</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">k</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.69444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.03148em;">k</span></span></span></span></span>)? Be as specific as you can!</p>
<p>1.7. You (Eve) have intercepted two ciphertexts:</p>
<p><span class="katex--display"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>c</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>=</mo><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mn>1111100101111001110011000001011110000110</mn></mstyle></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">

</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.58056em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">c</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.301108em;"><span class="" style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span class=""></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.277778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.277778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.64444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord" style="color: brown;">1111100101111001110011000001011110000110</span></span></span></span></span></span></p>
<p><span class="katex--display"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>c</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>=</mo><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mn>1111101001100111110111010000100110001000</mn></mstyle></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">

</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.58056em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">c</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.301108em;"><span class="" style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span class=""></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.277778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.277778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.64444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord" style="color: brown;">1111101001100111110111010000100110001000</span></span></span></span></span></span></p>
<p>You know that both are OTP ciphertexts, encrypted with the <em>same key</em>. You know that <strong>either</strong> <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>c</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">c_1</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.58056em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord text" style="color: brown;"><span class="mord texttt" style="color: brown;">delta</span></span></span></span></span></span> and <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>c</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">c_2</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.58056em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">c</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.301108em;"><span class="" style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span class=""></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> is an encryption of <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mtext mathvariant="monospace">gamma</mtext></mstyle></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\textcolor{brown}{\texttt{gamma}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.65278em; vertical-align: -0.22222em;"></span><span class="mord text" style="color: brown;"><span class="mord texttt" style="color: brown;">gamma</span></span></span></span></span></span> (all converted to binary from ascii in the standard way).<br>
Which of these two possibilities is correct, and why? What was the key <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>k</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">k</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.69444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.03148em;">k</span></span></span></span></span>?</p>
<p>1.8. A <strong>known-plaintext attack</strong> refers to a situation where an eavesdropper sees a ciphertext <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>c</mi><mo>=</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">c =</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.43056em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">c</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.277778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span></span></span></span></span> Enc<span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>k</mi><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi>m</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">(k,m)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.03148em;">k</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.166667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">m</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span> and also learns/knows what plaintext <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>m</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">m</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.43056em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">m</span></span></span></span></span> was used to generate <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>c</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">c</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.43056em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">c</span></span></span></span></span>.<br>
(a) Show that a known-plaintext attack on OTP results in the attacker learning the key <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>k</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">k</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.69444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.03148em;">k</span></span></span></span></span>.<br>
(b) Can OTP be secure if it allows an attacker to recover the encryption key? Is this a contradiction to the security we showed for OTP? Explain.</p>
<p>1.9. Suppose we modify the subroutine discussed in <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mstyle mathcolor="green"><mi>C</mi><mi>l</mi><mi>a</mi><mi>i</mi><mi>m</mi><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mn>1.3</mn></mstyle></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\textcolor{green}{Claim \ 1.3}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.69444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.01968em; color: green;">Cl</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="color: green;">aim</span><span class="mspace" style="color: green;"><span style="color: green;">&nbsp;</span></span><span class="mord" style="color: green;">1.3</span></span></span></span></span> so that it also returns <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>k</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">k</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.69444em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.03148em;">k</span></span></span></span></span>:</p>
<p><span class="katex--display"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><menclose notation="top bottom left right"><mtable rowspacing="0.6600em" columnalign="left" columnspacing="1em"><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><munder accentunder="true"><mrow><msup><mtext>&nbsp;EAVESDROP&nbsp;</mtext><mo mathvariant="normal" lspace="0em" rspace="0em">′</mo></msup><mrow><mo fence="true">(</mo><mi>m</mi><mo>∈</mo><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mn>0</mn></mstyle><mo separator="true">,</mo><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mn>1</mn></mstyle><msup><mo stretchy="false">}</mo><mi>λ</mi></msup><mo fence="true">)</mo></mrow><mo>:</mo></mrow><mo stretchy="true">‾</mo></munder></mstyle></mtd></mtr><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mrow><mspace width="1em"></mspace><mi>k</mi><mo>←</mo><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mn>0</mn></mstyle><mo separator="true">,</mo><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mn>1</mn></mstyle><msup><mo stretchy="false">}</mo><mi>λ</mi></msup></mrow></mstyle></mtd></mtr><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mrow><mspace width="1em"></mspace><mi>c</mi><mo>:</mo><mo>=</mo><mi>k</mi><mo>⊕</mo><mi>m</mi></mrow></mstyle></mtd></mtr><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mrow><mspace width="1em"></mspace><mtext>return&nbsp;</mtext><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mpadded width="+6pt" height="+6pt" lspace="3pt" voffset="3pt" mathbackground="yellow"><mtext>k</mtext></mpadded><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi>c</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mstyle></mtd></mtr></mtable></menclose><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi mathvariant="normal">.</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">

\begin{array}{|l|} \hline

\quad k \leftarrow\{\textcolor{brown}{0},\textcolor{brown}{1}\}^{\lambda} \\

<p>Is it still true that for every <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>m</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">m</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.43056em; Or is the output distribution different for different choice of <span class="katex--inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>m</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">m</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.43056em; vertical-align: 0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">m</span></span></span></span></span>?</p>
<p>1.10. In this problem we discuss the security of performing one-time pad encryption twice:<br>
(a) Consider the following subroutine that models the result of applying one-time pad encryption with two <em>independent</em> keys:</p>
<p><span class="katex--display"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><menclose notation="top bottom left right"><mtable rowspacing="0.6600em" columnalign="left" columnspacing="1em"><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><munder accentunder="true"><mrow><msup><mtext>&nbsp;EAVESDROP&nbsp;</mtext><mo mathvariant="normal" lspace="0em" rspace="0em">′</mo></msup><mrow><mo fence="true">(</mo><mi>m</mi><mo>∈</mo><mo fence="true">)</mo></mrow><mo>:</mo></mrow><mo stretchy="true">‾</mo></munder></mstyle></mtd></mtr><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mrow><mspace mathcolor="brown"><mn>1</mn></mstyle><msup><mo stretchy="false">}</mo><mi>λ</mi></msup></mrow></mstyle></mtd></mtr><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mrow><mspace width="1em"></mspace><msub><mi>k</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>←</mo><mo stretchy="false">{</mo><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mn>0</mn></mstyle><mo separator="true">,</mo><mstyle mathcolor="brown"><mn>1</mn></mstyle><msup><mo stretchy="false">}</mo><mi>λ</mi></msup></mrow></mstyle></mtd></mtr><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mrow><mspace width="1em"></mspace><mi>c</mi><mo>:</mo><mo>=</mo><msub><mi>k</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>⊕</mo><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>k</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>⊕</mo><mi>m</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mstyle></mtd></mtr><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mrow><mspace width="1em"></mspace><mtext>return&nbsp;</mtext><mi>c</mi></mrow></mstyle></mtd></mtr></mtable></menclose><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi mathvariant="normal">.</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
\def\arraystretch{1.5} 
\begin{array}{|l|} \hline
\underline{\text { EAVESDROP }^{\prime}\left(m \in\{\textcolor{brown}{0},\textcolor{brown}{1}\}^{\lambda}\right) :} \\
\quad k_1 \leftarrow\{\textcolor{brown}{0},\textcolor{brown}{1}\}^{\lambda} \\
\quad k_2 \leftarrow\{\textcolor{brown}{0},\textcolor{brown}{1}\}^{\lambda} \\
\quad c:=k_2 \oplus (k_1 \oplus m) \\
\quad \text {return } c \\ \hline
\end{array} \ .
</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 9.05001em; vertical-align: -4.255em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 4.79501em;"><span class="" style="top: -6.75501em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 6.75501em;"></span><span class="mtable"><span class="vertical-separator" style="height: 9.01001em;
